# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement the listener manager: the listener addition/removal API, the listener drain mechanism, the connection handler assignment to worker threads, and the listener socket sharing between workers.

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the Envoy listener manager architecture. The answer includes:

## Summary of Findings

I've identified **42 C++ source files** implementing the listener manager in envoyproxy/envoy (v1.31.2), including:

### Core Components:
1. **Listener Manager** - Central orchestrator (listener_manager_impl.h/cc)
2. **Listener Configuration** - ListenerImpl with ListenSocketFactoryImpl for socket management
3. **Connection Handler** - ConnectionHandlerImpl managing worker thread assignments
4. **Worker Threads** - WorkerImpl handling individual thread operations

### Listener Types:
- **TCP Listeners** - ActiveTcpListener with connection acceptance and balancing
- **UDP Listeners** - ActiveRawUdpListener with worker-based packet routing
- **QUIC Listeners** - ActiveQuicListener with BPF-based connection distribution
- **Internal Listeners** - ActiveInternalListener for internal communication

### Key Mechanisms:

**Listener Addition/Removal API:**
- `addOrUpdateListener()` - Handles listener creation, warming, and activation
- `removeListener()` - Initiates listener draining

**Drain Mechanism:**
- `DrainingListener` struct tracks workers pending removal
- `DrainManagerImpl` manages graceful drain sequences
- `DrainingFilterChainsManager` handles individual filter chain draining

**Connection Handler Assignment:**
- Each worker receives listeners via `WorkerImpl::addListener()`
- ConnectionHandlerImpl maintains listener-to-tag mappings
- ActiveListener instances created per worker for distributed connection handling

**Socket Sharing Between Workers:**
- ListenSocketFactoryImpl pre-creates sockets for all workers
- Reuse_port mode: unique socket per worker
- Non-reuse_port mode: socket duplicated from worker 0
- Each worker gets its o
... (truncated)

# Listener implementation\\n2: \\n3: ## Socket handling\\n4: \\n5: Envoy uses the following procedure for creating sockets and assigning them to workers.\\n6: \\n7: 1. When a listener is created, a socket is pre-created for every worker on the main thread. This\\n8:    allows most errors to be caught early on in the listener creation process (e.g., bad socket\\n9:    option, unable to bind, etc.).\\n10:     * If using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for every worker.\\n11:     * If not using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for worker 0, and then that socket\\n12:       is duplicated for all other workers.\\n13: 2. In the case of a listener update in which the address/socket is to be shared (i.e., a named\\n14:    listener that has configuration settings changed but listens on the same address will share\\n15:    sockets with the draining listener), all sockets are duplicated regardless of whether using\\n16:    reuse_port or not. This keeps the logic equivalent, and also makes sure that when using\\n17: \",\"endLine\":17,\"startLine\":1},{\"content\":\"17:    reuse_port no TCP connections are dropped during the drain process (in the race condition between\\n18:    assigning a queue and closing the listening socket on the old listener).\\n19: 3. In the case of hot restart, all sockets are requested by worker index. If the old process has\\n20:    a match, the socket is duplicated and sent to the new process. Thus, hot restart and a listener\\n21:    update effectively share the same update process. This is so that no connections are dropped\\n22: \",\"endLine\":22,\"startLine\":17},{\"content\":\"22:    when using reuse_port.\\n23: 4. A consequence of every listener having dedicated sockets (whether duplicated or not) is that\\n24:    a listener can close() its sockets when removed without concern for other listeners.\\n25: \\n26: For more information, see `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` and its use within `ListenerImpl` and\\n27: `ListenerManagerImpl`.\\n28: \",\"endLine\":28,\"startLine\":22}],\"file\":\"source/docs/listener.md\",\"repo\":\"github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2\",\"type\":\"file\",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2/-/blob/source/docs/listener.md\"},{\"chunks\":[{\"content\":\"745: \\n746: void ListenerManagerImpl::addListenerToWorker(Worker& worker,\\n747:                                               absl::optional<uint64_t> overridden_listener,\\n748:                                               ListenerImpl& listener,\\n749:                                               ListenerCompletionCallback completion_callback) {\\n750:   if (overridden_listener.has_value()) {\\n751:     ENVOY_LOG(debug, \\\"replacing existing listener {}\\\", overridden_listener.value());\\n752:   }\\n753:   worker.addListener(\\n754:       overridden_listener, listener,\\n755:       [this, completion_callback]() -> void {\\n756:         // The add listener completion runs on the worker thread.           {
            "content": "1: # Listener implementation\n2: \n3: ## Socket handling\n4: \n5: Envoy uses the following procedure for creating sockets and assigning them to workers.\n6: \n7: 1. When a listener is created, a socket is pre-created for every worker on the main thread. This\n8:    allows most errors to be caught early on in the listener creation process (e.g., bad socket\n9:    option, unable to bind, etc.).\n10:     * If using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for every worker.\n11:     * If not using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for worker 0, and then that socket\n12:       is duplicated for all other workers.\n13: 2. In the case of a listener update in which the address/socket is to be shared (i.e., a named\n14:    listener that has configuration settings changed but listens on the same address will share\n15:    sockets with the draining listener), all sockets are duplicated regardless of whether using\n16:    reuse_port or not. This keeps the logic equivalent, and also makes sure that when using\n17: ",
            "endLine": 17,
            "startLine": 1
          },
          {
            "content": "17:    reuse_port no TCP connections are dropped during the drain process (in the race condition between\n18:    assigning a queue and closing the listening socket on the old listener).\n19: 3. In the case of hot restart, all sockets are requested by worker index. If the old process has\n20:    a match, the socket is duplicated and sent to the new process. Thus, hot restart and a listener\n21:    update effectively share the same update process. This is so that no connections are dropped\n22: ",
            "endLine": 22,
            "startLine": 17
          },
          {
            "content": "22:    when using reuse_port.\n23: 4. A consequence of every listener having dedicated sockets (whether duplicated or not) is that\n24:    a listener can close() its sockets when removed without concern for other listeners.\n25: \n26: For more information, see `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` and its use within `ListenerImpl` and\n27: `ListenerManagerImpl`.\n28: ",
            "endLine": 28,

The architecture consists of several key components:\\n\\n## Core Listener Manager\\nThe `ListenerManager` interface (envoy/server/listener_manager.h) defines the public API for listener operations. The implementation is in `ListenerManagerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h/cc), which is the main orchestrator for:\\n1. **Listener Addition/Removal**: `addOrUpdateListener()` and `removeListener()` methods that handle listener lifecycle\\n2. **Listener Drain Mechanism**: `drainListener()` and `drainFilterChains()` manage graceful listener shutdown through the `DrainingListener` struct that tracks workers pending removal\\n\\n## Listener Configuration\\n`ListenerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/listener_impl.h/cc) represents individual listener configuration and integrates with `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` which manages socket creation and sharing between workers. The socket factory maintains separate sockets for each worker, handling both reuse_port (individual sockets per worker) and non-reuse_port (shared sockets) modes.\\n\\n## Connection Handler & Worker Thread Assignment\\n`ConnectionHandlerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/connection_handler_impl.h/cc) is the connection handler that runs on each worker thread and manages the assignment of listeners to worker threads. It maintains a mapping of listener tags to active listeners and handles connection acceptance.\\n\\n`WorkerImpl` (source/server/worker_impl.h/cc) represents a worker thread and receives listener additions from the main thread via `addListener()` method. Each worker has its own event dispatcher and connection handler.\\n\\n## Active Listener Types\\nThe listener manager supports multiple listener implementations:\\n- **TCP Listeners**: `ActiveTcpListener` (source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.h/cc) extends `OwnedActiveStreamListenerBase`\\n- **UDP Listeners**: `ActiveRawUdpListener` and `ActiveUdpListenerBase` (source/server/active_udp_listener.h/cc)\\n- **QUIC Listeners**: `ActiveQuicListener` and `ActiveQuicListenerFactory` (source/common/quic/active_quic_listener.h/cc)\\n- **Internal Listeners**: `ActiveInternalListener` (source/extensions/bootstrap/internal_listener/active_internal_listener.h/cc)\\n\\nAll these inherit from `ActiveListenerImplBase` (source/server/active_listener_base.h) which provides common listener statistics and lifecycle management.\\n\\n## Stream Listener Base\\n`ActiveStreamListenerBase` (source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.h/cc) and its subclass `OwnedActiveStreamListenerBase` provide the foundation for TCP and internal listeners, handling connection acceptance, filter chain management, and connection draining.\\n\\n## Drain Mechanism\\n`DrainManagerImpl` (source/server/drain_manager_impl.h/cc) handles the graceful draining of listeners. When listeners are marked for draining, they track `workers_pending_removal` and drain through a time period before complete removal. The `DrainingFilterChainsManager` (defined in source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h) manages individual filter chain draining.\\n\\n## Filter Chain Management\\n`FilterChainManagerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.h/cc) manages the set of filter chains within a listener and their selection based on connection properties. The `FilterChainFactoryContextCallback` and `ListenerFilterChainFactoryBuilder` (in source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h) build filter chains dynamically.\\n\\n## Socket Sharing Between Workers\\nSocket sharing is handled through `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` which pre-creates sockets for all workers during listener creation:\\n- For reuse_port: Creates unique sockets for each worker independently\\n- For non-reuse_port: Creates socket on worker 0 and duplicates for other workers\\nThis ensures socket sharing while allowing each worker to independently close its copy without affecting other workers or the overall listener.\\n\\n## Supporting Components\\n- **LdsApi**: `LdsApiImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/lds_api.h/cc) handles Listener Discovery Service (xDS) updates\\n- **Api Listeners**: `HttpApiListener` and `ApiListenerImplBase` (source/server/api_listener_impl.h/cc) for API-based listeners\\n- **Listener Hooks**: `ListenerHooks` (source/server/listener_hooks.h) provides callbacks for listener lifecycle events\\n- **Validation Listener Manager**: `ValidationListenerManager` (source/extensions/listener_managers/validation_listener_manager/) for configuration validation\\n- **Network Layer**: `TcpListenerImpl` and `UdpListenerImpl` (source/common/network/tcp_listener_impl.h/cc and udp_listener_impl.h/cc) provide the underlying network listener implementations\"\n}\n",

The socket factory maintains separate sockets for each worker, handling both reuse_port (individual sockets per worker) and non-reuse_port (shared sockets) modes.\\n\\n## Connection Handler & Worker Thread Assignment\\n`ConnectionHandlerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/connection_handler_impl.h/cc) is the connection handler that runs on each worker thread and manages the assignment of listeners to worker threads. It maintains a mapping of listener tags to active listeners and handles connection acceptance.\\n\\n`WorkerImpl` (source/server/worker_impl.h/cc) represents a worker thread and receives listener additions from the main thread via `addListener()` method. Each worker has its own event dispatcher and connection handler.\\n\\n## Active Listener Types\\nThe listener manager supports multiple listener implementations:\\n- **TCP Listeners**: `ActiveTcpListener` (source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.h/cc) extends `OwnedActiveStreamListenerBase`\\n- **UDP Listeners**: `ActiveRawUdpListener` and `ActiveUdpListenerBase` (source/server/active_udp_listener.h/cc)\\n- **QUIC Listeners**: `ActiveQuicListener` and `ActiveQuicListenerFactory` (source/common/quic/active_quic_listener.h/cc)\\n- **Internal Listeners**: `ActiveInternalListener` (source/extensions/bootstrap/internal_listener/active_internal_listener.h/cc)\\n\\nAll these inherit from `ActiveListenerImplBase` (source/server/active_listener_base.h) which provides common listener statistics and lifecycle management.\\n\\n## Stream Listener Base\\n`ActiveStreamListenerBase` (source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.h/cc) and its subclass `OwnedActiveStreamListenerBase` provide the foundation for TCP and internal listeners, handling connection acceptance, filter chain management, and connection draining.\\n\\n## Drain Mechanism\\n`DrainManagerImpl` (source/server/drain_manager_impl.h/cc) handles the graceful draining of listeners. When listeners are marked for draining, they track `workers_pending_removal` and drain through a time period before complete removal. The `DrainingFilterChainsManager` (defined in source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h) manages individual filter chain draining.\\n\\n## Filter Chain Management\\n`FilterChainManagerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.h/cc) manages the set of filter chains within a listener and their selection based on connection properties. The `FilterChainFactoryContextCallback` and `ListenerFilterChainFactoryBuilder` (in source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h) build filter chains dynamically.\\n\\n## Socket Sharing Between Workers\\nSocket sharing is handled through `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` which pre-creates sockets for all workers during listener creation:\\n- For reuse_port: Creates unique sockets for each worker independently\\n- For non-reuse_port: Creates socket on worker 0 and duplicates for other workers\\nThis ensures socket sharing while allowing each worker to independently close its copy without affecting other workers or the overall listener.\\n\\n## Supporting Components\\n- **LdsApi**: `LdsApiImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/lds_api.h/cc) handles Listener Discovery Service (xDS) updates\\n- **Api Listeners**: `HttpApiListener` and `ApiListenerImplBase` (source/server/api_listener_impl.h/cc) for API-based listeners\\n- **Listener Hooks**: `ListenerHooks` (source/server/listener_hooks.h) provides callbacks for listener lifecycle events\\n- **Validation Listener Manager**: `ValidationListenerManager` (source/extensions/listener_managers/validation_listener_manager/) for configuration validation\\n- **Network Layer**: `TcpListenerImpl` and `UdpListenerImpl` (source/common/network/tcp_listener_impl.h/cc and udp_listener_impl.h/cc) provide the underlying network listener implementations\"\n}\n",
